</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Languages</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">List of languages</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Time zones</th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%2B2" title="UTC+2">UTC+2</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%2B12" title="UTC+12">UTC+12</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Internet <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">TLD</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/.asia" title=".asia">.asia</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Largest cities</th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Asia" title="List of metropolitan areas in Asia">Metropolitan areas of Asia</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Asia" title="List of cities in Asia">List of cities in Asia</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/UN_M49" title="UN M49">UN M49 code</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><code>142</code> – Asia<br/><code>001</code> – World</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Populous_Asia_(physical,_political,_population)_with_legend.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4073" data-file-width="5819" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg/220px-Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg/330px-Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg/440px-Populous_Asia_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29_with_legend.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Populous_Asia_(physical,_political,_population)_with_legend.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the most populous part of Asia showing physical, political and population characteristics, as per 2018</div></div></div>
<p><b>Asia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ʒ/: 's' in 'pleasure'">ʒ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Asia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/En-us-Asia.ogg" title="En-us-Asia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>also <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a landmass, which is either considered a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> in its own right or a <a href="/wiki/Continent#Subcontinents" title="Continent">subcontinent</a> of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> which shares the continental <a href="/wiki/Landmass" title="Landmass">landmass</a> of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> with <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. Asia covers an area of 44,579,000 square kilometres (17,212,000 sq mi), about 30% of Earth's total land area and 8.7% of the Earth's total surface area. The continent, which has long been home to the majority of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_population" title="Human population">human population</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> was the site of many of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_civilization" title="First civilization">first civilizations</a>. Its 4.7 billion people<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> constitute roughly 60% of the world's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>In general terms, Asia is bounded on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, on the south by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, and on the north by the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>. The border of Asia with Europe is a historical and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_construct" title="Cultural construct">cultural construct</a>, as there is no clear physical and geographical separation between them. It is somewhat arbitrary and has moved since its first conception in <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>. The division of Eurasia into two continents reflects <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_dichotomy" title="East–West dichotomy">East–West</a> cultural, linguistic, and ethnic differences, some of which vary on a spectrum rather than with a sharp dividing line. A commonly accepted division places Asia to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> separating it from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>; and to the east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Straits" title="Turkish Straits">Turkish Straits</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, and to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Seas</a>, separating it from Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> alternated in being the <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_by_past_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of regions by past GDP (PPP)">largest economies in the world</a> from 1 to 1800 CE. China was a major economic power and attracted many to the east,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and for many the legendary wealth and prosperity of the ancient culture of India personified Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> attracting European commerce, exploration and colonialism. The accidental discovery of a trans-Atlantic route from Europe to America by Columbus while in search for a route to India demonstrates this deep fascination. The <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> became the main east–west trading route in the Asian hinterlands while the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Straits of Malacca</a> stood as a major sea route. Asia has exhibited economic dynamism (particularly East Asia) as well as robust population growth during the 20th century, but overall population growth has since fallen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Asia was the birthplace of most of the world's mainstream religions including <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, as well as many other religions.
</p><p>Given its size and diversity, the concept of Asia—a <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">name</a> dating back to <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>—may actually have more to do with <a href="/wiki/Human_geography" title="Human geography">human geography</a> than <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physical geography</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Asia varies greatly across and within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regions_of_Asia" title="Regions of Asia">its regions</a> with regard to ethnic groups, cultures, environments, economics, historical ties and government systems. It also has a mix of many different climates ranging from the equatorial south via the hot desert in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, temperate areas in the east and the  continental centre to vast subarctic and polar areas in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_boundaries">Definition and boundaries</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information on Asian borders: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Asia#Boundary" title="Geography of Asia">Geography of Asia § Boundary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_continents" title="Boundaries between continents">Boundaries between continents</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries#Asia_and_Europe" title="List of transcontinental countries">List of transcontinental countries § Asia and Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a></div>
<h3><span id="Asia.E2.80.93Africa_boundary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia–Africa_boundary">Asia–Africa boundary</span></h3>
<p>The boundary between Asia and Africa is the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Suez" title="Gulf of Suez">Gulf of Suez</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> This makes Egypt a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">transcontinental country</a>, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai_peninsula" title="Sinai peninsula">Sinai peninsula</a> in Asia and the remainder of the country in Africa.
</p>
<h3><span id="Asia.E2.80.93Europe_boundary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia–Europe_boundary">Asia–Europe boundary</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1129" data-file-width="729" decoding="async" height="341" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png/220px-Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png/330px-Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png/440px-Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Possible_definitions_of_the_boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Definitions used for the boundary between Europe and Asia in different periods of History. The commonly accepted <a href="#Modern_definition">modern definition</a> mostly fits with the lines "<b>B</b>" and "<b>F</b>" in this image.</div></div></div>
<p>The threefold division of the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a> into Europe, Asia and Africa has been in use since the 6th century BC, due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_geographers" title="Greek geographers">Greek geographers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Anaximander" title="Anaximander">Anaximander</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hecataeus_of_Miletus" title="Hecataeus of Miletus">Hecataeus</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Anaximander placed the boundary between Asia and Europe along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phasis_River" title="Phasis River">Phasis River</a> (the modern Rioni river) in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> of Caucasus (from its mouth by <a href="/wiki/Poti" title="Poti">Poti</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coast, through the <a href="/wiki/Surami_Pass" title="Surami Pass">Surami Pass</a> and along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura River</a> to the Caspian Sea), a convention still followed by <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> in the 5th century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> this convention was revised, and the boundary between Europe and Asia was now considered to be the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_River_(Russia)" title="Don River (Russia)">Tanais</a> (the modern Don River). This is the convention used by Roman era authors such as <a href="/wiki/Posidonius" title="Posidonius">Posidonius</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The border between Asia and Europe was historically defined by European academics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-24">[24]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_River_(Russia)" title="Don River (Russia)">Don River</a> became unsatisfactory to northern Europeans when <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, king of the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>, defeating rival claims of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> to the eastern lands, and armed resistance by the tribes of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, synthesized a new <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> extending to the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and beyond, founded in 1721.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In Sweden, five years after Peter's death, in 1730 <a href="/wiki/Philip_Johan_von_Strahlenberg" title="Philip Johan von Strahlenberg">Philip Johan von Strahlenberg</a> published a new atlas proposing the Ural Mountains as the border of Asia. Tatishchev announced that he had proposed the idea to von Strahlenberg. The latter had suggested the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emba_River" title="Emba River">Emba River</a> as the lower boundary. Over the next century various proposals were made until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a> prevailed in the mid-19th century. The border had been moved perforce from the Black Sea to the Caspian Sea into which the Ural River projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The border between the Black Sea and the Caspian is usually placed along the crest of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a>, although it is sometimes placed further north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Asia.E2.80.93Oceania_boundary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia–Oceania_boundary">Asia–Oceania boundary</span></h3>
<p>The border between Asia and the region of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> is usually placed somewhere in the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a> in Indonesia are often considered to lie on the border of southeast Asia, with <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, to the east of the islands, being wholly part of Oceania. The terms Southeast Asia and Oceania, devised in the 19th century, have had several vastly different geographic meanings since their inception. The chief factor in determining which islands of the Malay Archipelago are Asian has been the location of the colonial possessions of the various empires there (not all European). Lewis and Wigen assert, "The narrowing of 'Southeast Asia' to its present boundaries was thus a gradual process."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myth_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Myth-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ongoing_definition">Ongoing definition</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afro-Eurasia_(orthographic_projection)_political.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg/220px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg/330px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg/440px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29_political.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afro-Eurasia_(orthographic_projection)_political.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> shown in green</div></div></div>
<p>Geographical Asia is a cultural artifact of European conceptions of the world, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greeks</a>, being imposed onto other cultures, an imprecise concept causing endemic contention about what it means. Asia does not exactly correspond to the cultural borders of its various types of constituents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the time of <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> a minority of geographers have rejected the three-continent system (Europe, Africa, Asia) on the grounds that there is no substantial physical separation between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McG-H_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-McG-H-28">[28]</a></sup> For example, Sir <a href="/wiki/Barry_Cunliffe" title="Barry Cunliffe">Barry Cunliffe</a>, the emeritus professor of European archeology at Oxford, argues that Europe has been geographically and culturally merely "the western excrescence of the continent of Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Geographically, Asia is the major eastern constituent of the continent of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> with Europe being a northwestern <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> of the landmass. Asia, Europe and Africa make up a single continuous landmass—<a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> (except for the Suez Canal)—and share a common <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a>. Almost all of Europe and a major part of Asia sit atop the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>, adjoined on the south by the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">Arabian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Plate" title="Indian Plate">Indian Plate</a> and with the easternmost part of Siberia (east of the <a href="/wiki/Chersky_Range" title="Chersky Range">Chersky Range</a>) on the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulf5..JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/280px-Gulf5..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/420px-Gulf5..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/560px-Gulf5..JPG 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulf5..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ptolemy's Asia</div></div></div>
<p>The idea of a place called "Asia" was originally a concept of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_civilization" title="Greek civilization">Greek civilization</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-reid-30">[30]</a></sup> though this did not correspond to the entire continent currently known by that name (which was unknown to Greece at the time). The English word comes from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> literature, where it has the same form, "Asia". Whether "Asia" in other languages comes from Latin of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> is much less certain, and the ultimate source of the Latin word is uncertain, though several theories have been published. One of the first classical writers to use Asia as a name of the whole continent was <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonymical</a> change in meaning is common and can be observed in some other geographical names, such as <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">Bronze Age</span></h3>
<p>Before Greek poetry, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> area was in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Dark_Age" title="Greek Dark Age">Greek Dark Age</a>, at the beginning of which syllabic writing was lost and alphabetic writing had not begun. Prior to then in the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> the records of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Empire" title="Assyrian Empire">Assyrian Empire</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">Hittite Empire</a> and the various <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece" title="Mycenaean Greece">Mycenaean</a> states of Greece mention a region undoubtedly Asia, certainly in Anatolia, including if not identical to Lydia. These records are administrative and do not include poetry.
</p><p>The Mycenaean states were destroyed about 1200 BCE by unknown agents, though one school of thought assigns the <a href="/wiki/Dorian_invasion" title="Dorian invasion">Dorian invasion</a> to this time. The burning of the palaces caused the clay tablets holding the Mycenaean administrative records to be preserved by baking. These tablets were written in a Greek syllabic script called <a href="/wiki/Linear_B" title="Linear B">Linear B</a>. This script was deciphered by a number of interested parties, most notably by a young World War II cryptographer, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ventris" title="Michael Ventris">Michael Ventris</a>, subsequently assisted by the scholar, <a href="/wiki/John_Chadwick" title="John Chadwick">John Chadwick</a>.
</p><p>A major cache discovered by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Blegen" title="Carl Blegen">Carl Blegen</a> at the site of ancient <a href="/wiki/Pylos" title="Pylos">Pylos</a> included hundreds of male and female names formed by different methods. Some of these are of women held in servitude (as study of the society implied by the content reveals). They were used in trades, such as cloth-making, and usually came with children. The epithet <i>lawiaiai</i>, "captives", associated with some of them identifies their origin. Some are ethnic names. One in particular, <i>aswiai</i>, identifies "women of Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Perhaps they were captured in Asia, but some others, <i>Milatiai</i>, appear to have been of <a href="/wiki/Miletus" title="Miletus">Miletus</a>, a Greek colony, which would not have been raided for slaves by Greeks. Chadwick suggests that the names record the locations where these foreign women were purchased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The name is also in the singular, <i>Aswia</i>, which refers both to the name of a country and to a female from there. There is a masculine form, <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn">aswios</i></span>. This <i>Aswia</i> appears to have been a remnant of a region known to the Hittites as Assuwa, centered on <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydia</a>. This name, <i>Assuwa</i>, has been suggested as the origin for the name of the continent "Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assuwa_league" title="Assuwa league">Assuwa league</a> was a confederation of states in western Anatolia, defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittites</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tudhaliya_I" title="Tudhaliya I">Tudhaliya I</a> around 1400 BCE.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">Classical antiquity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_-_Asia_(125_AD).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1817" data-file-width="2186" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/220px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/330px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/440px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_-_Asia_(125_AD).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The province of <a href="/wiki/Asia_(Roman_province)" title="Asia (Roman province)">Asia</a> highlighted (in red) within the Roman Empire.</div></div></div>
<p>Latin Asia and Greek Ἀσία appear to be the same word. Roman authors translated Ἀσία as Asia. The Romans named a province <a href="/wiki/Asia_(Roman_province)" title="Asia (Roman province)">Asia</a>, located in western Anatolia (in modern-day Turkey). There was an Asia Minor and an Asia Major located in modern-day Iraq. As the earliest evidence of the name is Greek, it is likely circumstantially that Asia came from Ἀσία, but ancient transitions, due to the lack of literary contexts, are difficult to catch in the act. The most likely vehicles were the ancient geographers and historians, such as <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a>, who were all Greek. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> certainly evidences early and rich uses of the name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first continental use of Asia is attributed to Herodotus (about 440 BCE), not because he innovated it, but because his <i>Histories</i> are the earliest surviving prose to describe it in any detail. He defines it carefully,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> mentioning the previous geographers whom he had read, but whose works are now missing. By it he means <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persian Empire</a>, in contrast to Greece and Egypt.
</p><p>Herodotus comments that he is puzzled as to why three women's names were "given to a tract which is in reality one" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_(mythology)" title="Asia (mythology)">Asia</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libya_(mythology)" title="Libya (mythology)">Libya</a>, referring to Africa), stating that most Greeks assumed that Asia was named after the wife of <a href="/wiki/Prometheus" title="Prometheus">Prometheus</a> (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Hesione" title="Hesione">Hesione</a>), but that the <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydians</a> say it was named after Asies, son of Cotys, who passed the name on to a tribe at <a href="/wiki/Sardis" title="Sardis">Sardis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythology</a>, "Asia" (<i>Ἀσία</i>) or "Asie" (<i>Ἀσίη</i>) was the name of a "<a href="/wiki/Nymph" title="Nymph">Nymph</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Titan_(mythology)" title="Titan (mythology)">Titan</a> goddess of Lydia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In ancient Greek religion, places were under the care of female divinities, parallel to guardian angels. The poets detailed their doings and generations in allegoric language salted with entertaining stories, which subsequently playwrights transformed into classical Greek drama and became "Greek mythology". For example, <a href="/wiki/Hesiod" title="Hesiod">Hesiod</a> mentions the daughters of <a href="/wiki/Tethys_(mythology)" title="Tethys (mythology)">Tethys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanus" title="Oceanus">Ocean</a>, among whom are a "holy company", "who with the Lord <a href="/wiki/Apollo" title="Apollo">Apollo</a> and the Rivers have youths in their keeping".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Many of these are geographic: Doris, Rhodea, Europa, Asia. Hesiod explains:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>For there are three-thousand neat-ankled daughters of Ocean who are dispersed far and wide, and in every place alike serve the earth and the deep waters.</p></blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Iliad" title="Iliad">Iliad</a> (attributed by the ancient Greeks to <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>) mentions two Phrygians (the tribe that replaced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luvians" title="Luvians">Luvians</a> in Lydia) in the <a href="/wiki/Trojan_War" title="Trojan War">Trojan War</a> named <a href="/wiki/Asius_(mythology)" title="Asius (mythology)">Asios</a> (an adjective meaning "Asian");<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and also a marsh or lowland containing a marsh in Lydia as <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ασιος</span></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> According to many Muslims, the term came from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>'s Queen <a href="/wiki/Asiya" title="Asiya">Asiya</a>, the adoptive mother of <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sahih_Al-Bukhari_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sahih_Al-Bukhari-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Asia" title="History of Asia">History of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silkroutes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/280px-Silkroutes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/420px-Silkroutes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/560px-Silkroutes.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silkroutes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> connected civilizations across Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_dominions1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="938" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/280px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/420px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/560px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_dominions1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> at its greatest extent. The gray area is the later <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The history of Asia can be seen as the distinct histories of several peripheral coastal regions: East Asia, South Asia, Southeast Asia and the Middle East, linked by the interior mass of the Central Asian <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>.
The coastal periphery was home to some of the world's earliest known civilizations, each of them developing around fertile river valleys. The civilizations in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" title="Indus Valley">Indus Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> shared many similarities. These civilizations may well have exchanged technologies and ideas such as <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">wheel</a>. Other innovations, such as writing, seem to have been developed individually in each area. Cities, states and empires developed in these lowlands.
</p><p>The central steppe region had long been inhabited by horse-mounted nomads who could reach all areas of Asia from the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>. The earliest postulated expansion out of the steppe is that of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-Europeans</a>, who spread their languages into the Middle East, South Asia, and the borders of China, where the <a href="/wiki/Tocharians" title="Tocharians">Tocharians</a> resided. The northernmost part of Asia, including much of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, was largely inaccessible to the steppe nomads, owing to the dense forests, climate and <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>. These areas remained very sparsely populated.
</p><p>The center and the peripheries were mostly kept separated by mountains and deserts. The <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himalaya" title="Himalaya">Himalaya</a> mountains and the <a href="/wiki/Karakum_Desert" title="Karakum Desert">Karakum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi</a> deserts formed barriers that the steppe horsemen could cross only with difficulty. While the urban city dwellers were more advanced technologically and socially, in many cases they could do little in a military aspect to defend against the mounted hordes of the steppe. However, the lowlands did not have enough open grasslands to support a large horsebound force; for this and other reasons, the <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomads</a> who conquered states in China, India, and the Middle East often found themselves adapting to the local, more affluent societies.
</p><p>The Islamic <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a>'s defeats of the Byzantine and Persian empires led to West Asia and southern parts of Central Asia and western parts of South Asia under its control during <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">its conquests</a> of the 7th century. The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> conquered a large part of Asia in the 13th century, an area extending from China to Europe. Before the Mongol invasion, <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> reportedly had approximately 120 million citizens; the 1300 census which followed the invasion reported roughly 60 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, one of the most devastating <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemics</a> in human history, is thought to have originated in the arid plains of central Asia, where it then travelled along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> began to expand into Asia from the 17th century, and would eventually take control of all of Siberia and most of Central Asia by the end of the 19th century. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> controlled Anatolia, most of the Middle East, North Africa and the Balkans from the mid 16th century onwards. In the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a> conquered China and established the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>. The Islamic <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> and the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Maratha Empire</a> controlled much of India in the 16th and 18th centuries respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> controlled most of East Asia and much of Southeast Asia, New Guinea and the Pacific islands until the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Asia" title="Geography of Asia">Geography of Asia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Biota_of_Asia" title="Category:Biota of Asia">Category:Biota of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himalayas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1998" data-file-width="3032" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/220px-Himalayas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/330px-Himalayas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/440px-Himalayas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himalayas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayan</a> range is home to some of the planet's highest peaks.</div></div></div>
<p>Asia is the largest continent on Earth. It covers 9% of the Earth's total surface area (or 30% of its land area), and has the longest coastline, at 62,800 kilometres (39,022 mi). Asia is generally defined as comprising the eastern four-fifths of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>. It is located to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, and south of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> (or the <a href="/wiki/Kuma%E2%80%93Manych_Depression" title="Kuma–Manych Depression">Kuma–Manych Depression</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Seas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-49">[49]</a></sup> It is bounded on the east by the Pacific Ocean, on the south by the Indian Ocean and on the north by the Arctic Ocean. Asia is subdivided into 49 countries, five of them (<a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>) are <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental countries</a> lying partly in Europe. Geographically, Russia is partly in Asia, but is considered a <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Europe">European nation</a>, both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_culture" title="Russian culture">culturally</a> and politically.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a> stretches across much of the Middle East. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> in China is the longest river in the continent. The <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> between <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> and China is the tallest mountain range in the world. Tropical rainforests stretch across much of southern Asia and coniferous and deciduous forests lie farther north.
</p>

</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_regions">Main regions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="527" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png/320px-Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png/480px-Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Division of Asia into regions by the UNSD <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1022511316">.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key{column-count:2}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key-wide{column-count:3}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key-narrow{column-count:1}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key>ol{margin-left:1.3em;margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key>ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="plainlist image-key"><ul><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#0000E0; color:white;"> </span> North Asia</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#E000E0; color:black;"> </span> Central Asia</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#00E000; color:black;"> </span> Western Asia (Near East)</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#E00000; color:white;"> </span> South Asia</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFFF00; color:black;"> </span> East Asia (Far East)</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFC000; color:black;"> </span> Southeast Asia</div></li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p>There are various approaches to the regional division of Asia. The following subdivision into regions is used, among others, by the UN statistics agency <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNSD" title="UNSD">UNSD</a>. This division of Asia into regions by the United Nations is done solely for statistical reasons and does not imply any assumption about political or other affiliations of countries and territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[a]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">The 'stans</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> (The <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> or <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia" title="Mainland Southeast Asia">Indochina</a>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Asia" title="Climate of Asia">Climate of Asia</a></div>
<p>Asia has extremely diverse climate features. Climates range from arctic and subarctic in Siberia to tropical in southern India and Southeast Asia. It is moist across southeast sections, and dry across much of the interior. Some of the largest daily temperature ranges on Earth occur in western sections of Asia. The monsoon circulation dominates across southern and eastern sections, due to the presence of the Himalayas forcing the formation of a thermal low which draws in moisture during the summer. Southwestern sections of the continent are hot. Siberia is one of the coldest places in the Northern Hemisphere, and can act as a source of arctic air masses for North America. The most active place on Earth for tropical cyclone activity lies northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and south of Japan.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2126" data-file-width="3780" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png/220px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png/330px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png/440px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Temperature_Bar_Chart_Asia--1901-2020--2021-07-14.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing <a href="/wiki/Temperature_anomaly" title="Temperature anomaly">temperature change</a> in Asia from 1901 to 2021. <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> is having major impacts on many countries in the continent.</div></div></div>
<p>A survey carried out in 2010 by global risk analysis farm <a href="/wiki/Maplecroft" title="Maplecroft">Maplecroft</a> identified 16 countries that are extremely <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">vulnerable to climate change</a>. Each nation's vulnerability was calculated using 42 socio, economic and environmental indicators, which identified the likely climate change impacts during the next 30 years. The Asian countries of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Bangladesh" title="Climate change in Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_India" title="Climate change in India">India</a>, the Philippines, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Pakistan" title="Climate change in Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_China" title="Climate change in China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Climate change in Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> were among the 16 countries facing extreme risk from climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Some shifts are already occurring. For example, in tropical parts of India with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a>, the temperature increased by 0.4 °C between 1901 and 2003.
A 2013 study by the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (ICRISAT) aimed to find science-based, pro-poor approaches and techniques that would enable Asia's agricultural systems to cope with climate change, while benefitting poor and vulnerable farmers. The study's recommendations ranged from improving the use of climate information in local planning and strengthening weather-based agro-advisory services, to stimulating diversification of rural household incomes and providing incentives to farmers to adopt natural resource conservation measures to enhance forest cover, replenish groundwater and use <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>The ten countries of the Association of Southeast Asian Nations (ASEAN) – Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Cambodia" title="Climate change in Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Indonesia" title="Climate change in Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, Laos, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Malaysia" title="Climate change in Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Myanmar, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Philippines" title="Climate change in the Philippines">the Philippines</a>, Singapore, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Thailand" title="Climate change in Thailand">Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Vietnam" title="Climate change in Vietnam">Vietnam</a> – are among the most vulnerable to the effects of climate change in the world, however, ASEAN's climate mitigation efforts are not commensurate with the climate threats and risks it faces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Asia" title="Economy of Asia">Economy of Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_countries_by_GDP" title="List of Asian countries by GDP">List of Asian countries by GDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_in_Asia-Pacific_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries in Asia-Pacific by GDP (nominal)">List of countries in Asia-Pacific by GDP (nominal)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_and_Pacific_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of Asian and Pacific countries by GDP (PPP)">List of Asian and Pacific countries by GDP (PPP)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1703" data-file-width="4036" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg/280px-1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg/420px-1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg/560px-1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_Singapore_city_skyline_2010_day_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Singapore has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports" title="List of busiest container ports">busiest container ports in the world</a> and is the world's fourth largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> trading center.</div></div></div>
<p>Asia has the largest continental economy by both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">Nominal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> in the world, and is the fastest growing economic region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the largest economies in Asia are China, Japan, India, South Korea, Indonesia and Turkey based on GDP in both nominal and PPP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Based on Global Office Locations 2011, Asia dominated the office locations with 4 of the top 5 being in Asia: Hong Kong, Singapore, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>. Around 68 percent of international firms have an office in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 1990s and early 2000s, the economies of China<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> and India grew rapidly, both with an average annual growth rate of more than 8%. Other recent very-high-growth nations in Asia include Israel, Malaysia, Indonesia, Bangladesh, Thailand, Vietnam, and the Philippines, and mineral-rich nations such as Kazakhstan, Turkmenistan, Iran, Brunei, the United Arab Emirates, Qatar, Kuwait, Saudi Arabia, Bahrain and Oman.
</p><p>According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_historian" title="Economic historian">economic historian</a> <a href="/wiki/Angus_Maddison" title="Angus Maddison">Angus Maddison</a> in his book <i>The World Economy: A Millennial Perspective</i>, India had the world's largest economy during 0 BCE and 1000 BCE. Historically, India was the largest economy in the world for most of the two millennia from the 1st until 19th century, contributing 25% of the world's industrial output.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> China was the <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_China" title="Economic history of China">largest and most advanced economy</a> on earth for much of recorded history and shared the mantle with India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> For several decades in the late twentieth century Japan was the largest economy in Asia and second-largest of any single nation in the world, after surpassing the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (measured in net material product) in 1990 and Germany in 1968. (NB: A number of supernational economies are larger, such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/APEC" title="APEC">APEC</a>). This ended in 2010 when China overtook Japan to become the world's second largest economy.
</p><p>In the late 1980s and early 1990s, Japan's GDP was almost as large (current exchange rate method) as that of the rest of Asia combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In 1995, Japan's economy nearly equaled that of the US as the largest economy in the world for a day, after the Japanese currency reached a record high of 79 <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">yen</a>/US$. Economic growth in Asia since World War II to the 1990s had been concentrated in Japan as well as the four regions of South Korea, Taiwan, Hong Kong and Singapore located in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian tigers</a>, which have now all received developed country status, having the highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="707" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg/220px-Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg/330px-Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg/440px-Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_skyline_BWSL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mumbai is one of the most populous cities on the continent. The city is an infrastructure and tourism hub, and plays a crucial role in the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">economy of India</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>It is forecasted that India will overtake Japan in terms of nominal GDP by 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> By 2027, according to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, China will have the largest economy in the world. Several trade blocs exist, with the most developed being the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a>.
</p><p>Asia is the largest continent in the world by a considerable margin, and it is rich in natural resources, such as petroleum, forests, fish, water, rice, copper and silver. Manufacturing in Asia has traditionally been strongest in East and Southeast Asia, particularly in China, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, South Korea, Japan, India, the Philippines, and Singapore. Japan and South Korea continue to dominate in the area of <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporations</a>, but increasingly the PRC and India are making significant inroads. Many companies from Europe, North America, South Korea and Japan have operations in Asia's developing countries to take advantage of its abundant supply of cheap labour and relatively developed infrastructure.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> 9 of 11 <a href="/wiki/3G_(countries)" title="3G (countries)">Global Growth Generators</a> countries came from Asia driven by population and income growth. They are <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, China, India, Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, Mongolia, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Asia has three main financial centers: Hong Kong, Tokyo and Singapore. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Call_center" title="Call center">Call centers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" title="Business process outsourcing">business process outsourcing</a> (BPOs) are becoming major employers in India and the Philippines due to the availability of a large pool of highly skilled, English-speaking workers. The increased use of outsourcing has assisted the rise of India and the China as financial centers. Due to its large and extremely competitive information technology industry, India has become a major hub for outsourcing.
</p><p>Trade between Asian countries and countries on other continents is largely carried out on the sea routes that are important for Asia. Individual main routes have emerged from this. The main route leads from the Chinese coast south via Hanoi to Jakarta, Singapore and Kuala Lumpur through the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a> via the Sri Lankan Colombo to the southern tip of India via Malé to East Africa <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, from there to <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, then through the Red Sea over the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> into Mediterranean, there via Haifa, Istanbul and <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> to the upper Adriatic to the northern Italian hub of <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> with its rail connections to Central and Eastern Europe or further to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and around Spain and France to the European northern ports. A far smaller part of the goods traffic runs via South Africa to Europe. A particularly significant part of the Asian goods traffic is carried out across the Pacific towards <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_Beach" title="Long Beach">Long Beach</a>. In contrast to the sea routes, the Silk Road via the land route to Europe is on the one hand still under construction and on the other hand is much smaller in terms of scope. Intra-Asian trade, including sea trade, is growing rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Asia had 3.3 million millionaires (people with net worth over US$1 million excluding their homes), slightly below North America with 3.4 million millionaires. Last year Asia had toppled Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup>
Citigroup in The Wealth Report 2012 stated that Asian centa-millionaire overtook North America's wealth for the first time as the world's "economic center of gravity" continued moving east. At the end of 2011, there were 18,000 Asian people mainly in Southeast Asia, China and Japan who have at least $100 million in disposable assets, while North America with 17,000 people and Western Europe with 14,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h2>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/%E0%B8%A7%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%9E%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%95%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1-5.jpg/330px-%E0%B8%A7%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%9E%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%95%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/%E0%B8%A7%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%9E%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%95%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1-5.jpg/440px-%E0%B8%A7%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%9E%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%95%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1-5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B8%A7%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%9E%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%95%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%A8%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%94%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1-5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wat_Phra_Kaew" title="Wat Phra Kaew">Wat Phra Kaew</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Palace" title="Grand Palace">Grand Palace</a> is among <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>'s major tourist attractions.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref" role="note">See also the categories <a href="/wiki/Category:Tourism_in_Asia" title="Category:Tourism in Asia">Tourism in Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Transport_in_Asia" title="Category:Transport in Asia">Transport in Asia</a></div>
<p>With growing Regional Tourism with domination of Chinese visitors, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> has released Global Destination Cities Index 2013 with 10 of 20 are dominated by Asia and Pacific Region Cities and also for the first time a city of a country from Asia (<a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>) set in the top-ranked with 15.98 international visitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
