(PDF).</a><br/>The figure for 2021 is provided by the 2022 revision of the World Population Prospects<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2022_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2022-3">[3]</a></sup>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WorldPopulation.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="916" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/280px-WorldPopulation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/420px-WorldPopulation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/560px-WorldPopulation.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WorldPopulation.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing population by continent as a percentage of <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> (1750–2005)</div></div></div>
<p>East Asia had by far the strongest overall <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) improvement of any region in the world, nearly doubling average HDI attainment over the past 40 years, according to the report's analysis of health, education and income data. China, the second highest achiever in the world in terms of HDI improvement since
1970, is the only country on the "Top 10 Movers" list due to income rather than health or education achievements. Its per capita income increased a stunning 21-fold over the last four decades, also lifting hundreds of millions out of income poverty. Yet it was not among the region's top performers in improving school enrollment and life expectancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-83">[82]</a></sup>
<br/><a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, a South Asian country, emerges as one of the world's fastest movers since 1970 mainly due to health and education achievements. Its present <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is 25 years longer than in the 1970s. More than four of every five children of school age in Nepal now attend primary school, compared to just one in five 40 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-83">[82]</a></sup>
<br/> Hong Kong ranked highest among the countries grouped on the HDI (number 7 in the world, which is in the "very high human development" category), followed by Singapore (9), Japan (19) and South Korea (22). <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (155) ranked lowest amongst Asian countries out of the 169 countries assessed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-83">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">Languages of Asia</a></div>
<p>Asia is home to several <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language families</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolates</a>. Most Asian countries have more than one language that is natively spoken. For instance, according to <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a>, more than 600 languages are spoken in Indonesia, more than 800 languages spoken in India, and more than 100 are spoken in the Philippines. China has many languages and dialects in different provinces.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_philosophy" title="Eastern philosophy">Eastern philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Asia" title="Religion in Asia">Religion in Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_mythologies" title="List of Asian mythologies">List of Asian mythologies</a></div>
<p>Many of the world's <a href="/wiki/Major_religious_groups" title="Major religious groups">major religions</a> have their origins in Asia, including the five most practiced in the world (excluding <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">irreligion</a>), which are Christianity, Islam, Hinduism, Chinese folk religion (classified as Confucianism and Taoism), and Buddhism respectively. Asian mythology is complex and diverse. The story of the <a href="/wiki/Flood_myth" title="Flood myth">Great Flood</a> for example, as presented to Jews in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a> in the narrative of <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>—and later to Christians in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslims</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>—is earliest found in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_mythology" title="Mesopotamian mythology">Mesopotamian mythology</a>, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En%C3%BBma_Eli%C5%A1" title="Enûma Eliš">Enûma Eliš</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">Epic of Gilgamesh</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a> similarly tells about an <a href="/wiki/Avatar" title="Avatar">avatar</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a> in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Matsya" title="Matsya">fish</a> who warned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sraddhadeva_Manu" title="Sraddhadeva Manu">Manu</a> of a terrible flood. Ancient <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mythology" title="Chinese mythology">Chinese mythology</a> also tells of a <a href="/wiki/Great_Flood_(China)" title="Great Flood (China)">Great Flood</a> spanning generations, one that required the combined efforts of emperors and divinities to control.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Abrahamic">Abrahamic</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Asia" title="Christianity in Asia">Christianity in Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Asia" title="Islam in Asia">Islam in Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westernwall2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/220px-Westernwall2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/330px-Westernwall2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/440px-Westernwall2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westernwall2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">Western Wall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">Dome of the Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Church_of_the_Nativity_(7703592746).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg/220px-Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg/330px-Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg/440px-Church_of_the_Nativity_%287703592746%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Church_of_the_Nativity_(7703592746).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nativity" title="Church of the Nativity">Church of the Nativity</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/220px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/330px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/440px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pilgrims in the annual <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaabah" title="Kaabah">Kaabah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic religions</a> including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Druze_faith" title="Druze faith">Druze faith</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheDruze_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheDruze-84">[83]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> originated in West Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, the oldest of the Abrahamic faiths, is practiced primarily in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> homeland and historical birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Hebrew nation</a>: which today consists both of those <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> who remained in <a href="/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews" title="Mizrahi Jews">the Middle East</a> and those who returned from <a href="/wiki/Jewish_diaspora" title="Jewish diaspora">diaspora</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">North America</a>, and other regions;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> though various diaspora communities persist worldwide. Jews are the predominant ethnic group in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> (75.6%) numbering at about 6.1 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> although the levels of adherence to Jewish religion vary. Outside of Israel there are small ancient Jewish communities in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (17,400),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary-89">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> (9,100),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mashke2_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-mashke2-90">[89]</a></sup> Iran (8,756),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IranCensusMurder_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-IranCensusMurder-91">[90]</a></sup> India (5,000) and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> (4,000),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> among many other places. In total, there are 14.4–17.5 million (2016, est.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Jews alive in the world today, making them one of the smallest Asian minorities, at roughly 0.3 to 0.4 percent of the total population of the continent.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is a widespread religion in Asia with more than 286 million adherents according to <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> and nearly 364 million according to <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Britannica</a> Book of the Year 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> Constituting around 12.6% of the total population of Asia. In the Philippines and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> is the predominant religion;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-96">[95]</a></sup> it was introduced by the Spaniards and the Portuguese, respectively. In <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> and Georgia, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> is the predominant religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-96">[95]</a></sup> In the Middle East, such as in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fars_(territory)" title="Fars (territory)">Fars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Christianity" title="Syriac Christianity">Syriac Christianity</a> (<a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">Church of the East</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a> are prevalent minority denominations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HindsonMitchell2013_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-HindsonMitchell2013-97">[96]</a></sup> which are both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Christian" title="Eastern Christian">Eastern Christian</a> sects mainly adhered to <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrian people</a> or Syriac Christians. Vibrant indigenous minorities in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> are adhering to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-96">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Christians" title="Saint Thomas Christians">Saint Thomas Christians</a> in India trace their origins to the evangelistic activity of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_the_Apostle" title="Thomas the Apostle">Thomas the Apostle</a> in the 1st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Significant Christian communities also found in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-96">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, which originated in the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> located in modern-day Saudi Arabia, is the second largest and most widely-spread religion in Asia with at least 1 billion Muslims constituting around 23.8% of the total population of Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> With 12.7% of the world Muslim population, the country currently with the largest Muslim population in the world is Indonesia, followed by Pakistan (11.5%), India (10%), <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, Iran and Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holiest_sites_in_Islam#Jerusalem" title="Holiest sites in Islam">Jerusalem</a> are the three holiest cities for Islam in all the world. The <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a> attract large numbers of Muslim devotees from all over the world to Mecca and Medina. Iran is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27a" title="Shi'a">Shi'a</a> country.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> Faith or Druzism originated in Western Asia, is a monotheistic religion based on the teachings of figures like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamza_ibn-%27Ali_ibn-Ahmad" title="Hamza ibn-'Ali ibn-Ahmad">Hamza ibn-'Ali ibn-Ahmad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Hakim_bi-Amr_Allah" title="Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah">Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah</a>, and Greek <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>. The number of <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> people worldwide is around one million, with about 45% to 50% live in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, 35% to 40% live in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, and less than 10% live in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, with recently there has been a growing Druze diaspora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> originated in Asia, in Iran (Persia), and spread from there to the Ottoman Empire, Central Asia, India, and Burma during the lifetime of Bahá'u'lláh. Since the middle of the 20th century, growth has particularly occurred in other Asian countries, because Baháʼí activities in many Muslim countries has been <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Baháʼís">severely suppressed</a> by authorities. <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a> is a big Baháʼí Temple in India.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_and_East_Asian_religions">Indian and East Asian religions</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akshardham_Lotus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="327" data-file-width="435" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg/220px-Akshardham_Lotus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg/330px-Akshardham_Lotus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akshardham_Lotus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swaminarayan_Hinduism" title="Swaminarayan Hinduism">Swaminarayan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akshardham_(Delhi)" title="Akshardham (Delhi)">Akshardham Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Records</a> is the <i>World's Largest Comprehensive Hindu Temple</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Almost all Asian religions have philosophical character and Asian philosophical traditions cover a large spectrum of philosophical thoughts and writings. <a href="/wiki/Indian_philosophy" title="Indian philosophy">Indian philosophy</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Hindu_philosophy" title="Hindu philosophy">Hindu philosophy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_philosophy" title="Buddhist philosophy">Buddhist philosophy</a>. They include elements of nonmaterial pursuits, whereas another school of thought from India, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C4%81rv%C4%81ka" title="Cārvāka">Cārvāka</a>, preached the enjoyment of the material world. The religions of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> originated in India, South Asia. In East Asia, particularly in China and Japan, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen Buddhism</a> took shape.
</p><p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Hinduism has around 1.1 billion adherents. The faith represents around 25% of Asia's population and is the largest religion in Asia. However, it is mostly concentrated in South Asia. Over 80% of the populations of both India and Nepal adhere to Hinduism, alongside significant communities in Bangladesh, Pakistan, Bhutan, Sri Lanka and <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, Indonesia. Many overseas Indians in countries such as Burma, Singapore and Malaysia also adhere to Hinduism.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2600" data-file-width="3928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg/220px-Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg/330px-Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg/440px-Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_Wat_reflejado_en_un_estanque_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hindu-Buddhist temple of <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, the largest religious monument in the world</div></div></div>
<p>Buddhism has a great following in mainland Southeast Asia and East Asia. Buddhism is the religion of the majority of the populations of <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> (96%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> (95%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a> (80–89%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Japan (36–96%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> (75–84%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (70%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> (60–67%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (53–93%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (35–93%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> South Korea (23–50%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (19–21%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> (9–11%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (10–75%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> China (20–50%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (2–14%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> and small communities in India and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. The Communist-governed countries of China, Vietnam and North Korea are officially atheist, thus the number of Buddhists and other religious adherents may be under-reported.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> is found mainly in India and in overseas Indian communities such as the United States and Malaysia. <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> is found in Northern India and amongst overseas Indian communities in other parts of Asia, especially Southeast Asia. <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> is found predominantly in Mainland China, South Korea, Taiwan and in overseas Chinese populations. <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> is found mainly in Mainland China, Taiwan, Malaysia and Singapore. In many Chinese communities, Taoism is easily syncretized with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a>, thus exact religious statistics are difficult to obtain and may be understated or overstated.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_conflicts">Modern conflicts</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="873" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg/220px-A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg/330px-A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg/440px-A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_refugee_special_train_at_Ambala_Station_during_partition_of_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A refugee special train in Ambala, <a href="/wiki/Punjab" title="Punjab">Punjab</a> during the partition of India in 1947</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:June9protestTreefong01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1620" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/June9protestTreefong01.jpg/310px-June9protestTreefong01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/June9protestTreefong01.jpg/465px-June9protestTreefong01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/June9protestTreefong01.jpg/620px-June9protestTreefong01.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:June9protestTreefong01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Demonstrations in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2019_Hong_Kong_extradition_bill" title="2019 Hong Kong extradition bill">Extradition bill</a> began in March 2019 and turned into continuing mass movements, drawing around 2 million protesters by June</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Asia" title="Culture of Asia">Culture of Asia</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_prizes">Nobel prizes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1071" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg/170px-Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg/255px-Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg/340px-Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indian polymath <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a> was awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a> in 1913, and became Asia's first <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> laureate.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali</a> poet, dramatist, and writer from <a href="/wiki/Santiniketan" title="Santiniketan">Santiniketan</a>, now in <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, India, became in 1913 the first Asian <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureate</a>. He won his <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> for notable impact his prose works and poetic thought had on English, French, and other national literatures of Europe and the Americas. He is also the writer of the national anthems of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and India.
</p><p>Other Asian writers who won Nobel Prize for literature include <a href="/wiki/Yasunari_Kawabata" title="Yasunari Kawabata">Yasunari Kawabata</a> (Japan, 1968), <a href="/wiki/Kenzabur%C5%8D_%C5%8Ce" title="Kenzaburō Ōe">Kenzaburō Ōe</a> (Japan, 1994), <a href="/wiki/Gao_Xingjian" title="Gao Xingjian">Gao Xingjian</a> (China, 2000), <a href="/wiki/Orhan_Pamuk" title="Orhan Pamuk">Orhan Pamuk</a> (Turkey, 2006), and <a href="/wiki/Mo_Yan" title="Mo Yan">Mo Yan</a> (China, 2012). Some may consider the American writer, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_S._Buck" title="Pearl S. Buck">Pearl S. Buck</a>, an honorary Asian Nobel laureate, having spent considerable time in China as the daughter of missionaries, and based many of her novels, namely <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Earth" title="The Good Earth">The Good Earth</a></i> (1931) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mother_(1934_novel)" title="The Mother (1934 novel)">The Mother</a></i> (1933), as well as the biographies of her parents for their time in China, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Exile_(1936_book)" title="The Exile (1936 book)">The Exile</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Fighting_Angel" title="Fighting Angel">Fighting Angel</a></i>, all of which earned her the Literature prize in 1938.
</p><p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a> of India and <a href="/wiki/Shirin_Ebadi" title="Shirin Ebadi">Shirin Ebadi</a> of Iran were awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for their significant and pioneering efforts for democracy and human rights, especially for the rights of women and children. Ebadi is the first Iranian and the first Muslim woman to receive the prize. Another Nobel Peace Prize winner is <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> from <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Burma</a> for her peaceful and non-violent struggle under a military dictatorship in Burma. She is a nonviolent pro-democracy activist and leader of the National League for Democracy in Burma (Myanmar) and a noted prisoner of conscience. She is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> and was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize in 1991. Chinese dissident <a href="/wiki/Liu_Xiaobo" title="Liu Xiaobo">Liu Xiaobo</a> was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for "his long and non-violent struggle for fundamental human rights in China" on 8 October 2010. He is the first Chinese citizen to be awarded a Nobel Prize of any kind while residing in China. In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Kailash_Satyarthi" title="Kailash Satyarthi">Kailash Satyarthi</a> from India and <a href="/wiki/Malala_Yousafzai" title="Malala Yousafzai">Malala Yousafzai</a> from Pakistan were awarded the Nobel Peace Prize "for their struggle against the suppression of children and young people and for the right of all children to education".
</p><p>Sir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.V._Raman" title="C.V. Raman">C.V. Raman</a> is the first Asian to get a Nobel prize in Sciences. He won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> "for his work on the scattering of light and for the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Raman_scattering" title="Raman scattering">effect named after him</a>".
</p><p>Japan has won the most Nobel Prizes of any Asian nation with 24 followed by India which has won 13.
</p><p>Amartya Sen, (born 3 November 1933) is an Indian economist who was awarded the 1998 Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences for his contributions to welfare economics and <a href="/wiki/Social_choice_theory" title="Social choice theory">social choice theory</a>, and for his interest in the problems of society's poorest members.
</p><p>Other Asian Nobel Prize winners include <a href="/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar" title="Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar">Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdus_Salam" title="Abdus Salam">Abdus Salam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malala_Yousafzai" title="Malala Yousafzai">Malala Yousafzai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aumann" title="Robert Aumann">Robert Aumann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">Menachem Begin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Ciechanover" title="Aaron Ciechanover">Aaron Ciechanover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avram_Hershko" title="Avram Hershko">Avram Hershko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kahneman" title="Daniel Kahneman">Daniel Kahneman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">Shimon Peres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ada_Yonath" title="Ada Yonath">Ada Yonath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ramos-Horta" title="José Ramos-Horta">José Ramos-Horta</a> and Bishop <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Filipe_Ximenes_Belo" title="Carlos Filipe Ximenes Belo">Carlos Filipe Ximenes Belo</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timor_Leste" title="Timor Leste">Timor Leste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Dae-jung" title="Kim Dae-jung">Kim Dae-jung</a>, and 13 Japanese scientists. Most of the said awardees are from Japan and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> except for Chandrasekhar and Raman (India), Abdus Salam and Malala Yousafzai, (Pakistan), Arafat (Palestinian Territories), Kim (South Korea), and Horta and Belo (Timor Leste).
</p><p>In 2006, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a>, a community development bank that lends money to poor people, especially women in Bangladesh. Dr. Yunus received his PhD in economics from Vanderbilt University, United States. He is internationally known for the concept of micro credit which allows poor and destitute people with little or no collateral to borrow money. The borrowers typically pay back money within the specified period and the incidence of default is very low.
</p><p>The Dalai Lama has received approximately eighty-four awards over his spiritual and political career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> On 22 June 2006, he became one of only four people ever to be recognized with Honorary Citizenship by the Governor General of Canada. On 28 May 2005, he received the Christmas Humphreys Award from the Buddhist Society in the United Kingdom. Most notable was the Nobel Peace Prize, presented in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> on 10 December 1989.
</p>

<tbody><tr>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Siberia lies in Asia geographically, but is considered a part of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> culturally and politically.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-transcon-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-transcon_123-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-transcon_123-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-transcon_123-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-transcon_123-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-transcon_123-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russia is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental country</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Asia" title="Northern Asia">Northern Asia</a>, but is considered European historically, culturally, ethnically, and politically, and the vast majority of its population (78%) lives within its <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European part</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Moscow is located in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-126">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Turkey is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">transcontinental country</a> located mainly in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> with a smaller portion in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

"And [Asia] is connected to Europe by the land-strait between Lake Maiotis and the Sarmatian Ocean where the river Tanais crosses through."</span>
